Defending the Vision of Allah in Paradise
Author defends vision of Allah against objection of diminished pleasure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that the removal of the vision of Allah in Paradise diminishes blessings, and how he uses an analogy and a counter-argument to defend the doctrine.

Core Idea
Removal of one pleasure leads to another, not to loss.

This passage from al-Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla tackles a key objection to the vision of Allah in Paradise: if the vision is the supreme pleasure, then its absence would reduce the joy of the afterlife. The author responds with a nuanced argument that the pleasure of vision is replaced by other delights, and he turns the logic back on the objectors using the example of the Prophet's vision. Let's follow the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully alongside the literal translation. Notice the dialogue structure and the flow of the argument.
The passage is dense; read it twice to grasp the logical moves.
2
Identify the initial hypothetical dialogue about weakness
The passage opens with a conditional argument: if the opponent says 'Yes' to a question about weakness being removed, the author forces them to either admit vision or give an inconsistent answer.
This part sets up the groundwork for the main objection.
3
Understand the main objection about diminished pleasure
The opponent claims that if vision of Allah is the greatest pleasure, then losing it would be a decrease in blessings. The author distinguishes between proving the Essence is visible (which is the real issue) and the actual occurrence of vision.
Note that the author redirects the argument to the core theological point.
4
Analyze the author's response: compensation and turning the tables
The author argues that if one is turned away from seeing Allah, Allah creates an equal or greater pleasure (e.g., eating, drinking), so it's an increase. Then he turns the argument: the same logic applies to the Prophet's vision, and whatever the opponent says about that applies to Allah.
The analogy of a thousand dinars plus a dirham illustrates the idea of addition, not subtraction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قالوا نعم. قيل : إذا ارتفع الضعف هل نرى؟ فإن قالوا: لا قيل لم وقد زال المانع ؟ وإن قالوا: نعم، فقد رجعوا إلى الحق وأثبتوا الرؤية مع وجود الدقة فالانعدام حيث تنعدم لا يكون مضافا إلى الدقة بل على وجود ضد الرؤية، والله الموفق. والجواب عن قولهم : أن الرؤية عندكم كانت بطريقة الثواب ولذاتها فوق سائر اللذات، بزوالها تنتقص النعم . على ما قرروا أنا لو فرضنا الكلام في إثبات كون الذات مرئيا لا في وجود الرؤية لا محالة في دار الجزاء اندفع الإلزام، ثم نقول : ليس الأمر على ما زعمتم أنه إذا انصرف عن رؤية الله تعالى على معنى أن الله يخلق ضد رؤيته في أبصارهم تنعدم اللذة بل توجد وينصرف بتلك اللذة إلى لذة الأكل والشراب والنكاح، فهم يرجعون إلى زيادة لا إلى نقصان، وهذا كرجل يهب له واهب ألف دينار ثم يهب له بعد ذلك درهما، فالدرهم مع ألف من الدنانير أفضل من ألف وحدة. ثم يقلب عليهم هذا السؤال فيقال لهم: إذا كانت لذة رؤية النبي عليه السلام من أفضل لذات الجنة فيجب إذا رجعوا عن رؤيته إن يرجعوا إلى نقصان، فكل ما أجابوا به عنه فهو جوابنا لهم.
And if they say: Yes. It is said: When the weakness is removed, will we see? If they say: No, it is said: Why, when the obstacle has ceased? And if they say: Yes, then they have returned to the truth and affirmed vision with the existence of the opposite. For non-existence when it ceases is not attributed to the opposite, but to the existence of the opposite of vision, and Allah is the granter of success. And the answer to their statement: that vision for you was in the mode of reward, and its pleasure is above all other pleasures; by its removal blessings are diminished. According to what they established: if we had supposed speech about proving that the Essence is visible, not about the existence of vision necessarily in the abode of recompense, the objection would be repelled. Then we say: The matter is not as you claimed, that when one is turned away from seeing Allah Almighty, in the sense that Allah creates an opposite of His vision in their eyes, the pleasure ceases; rather it exists, and he turns with that pleasure to the pleasure of eating, drinking, and marriage. So they return to increase, not to decrease. And this is like a man to whom a giver grants a thousand dinars, then after that grants him a dirham; so the dirham along with a thousand dinars is better than just a thousand. Then this question is turned back upon them, and it is said to them: If the pleasure of seeing the Prophet, peace be upon him, is among the best pleasures of Paradise, then if they turn away from seeing him, they must return to decrease. So whatever they answer about that is our answer to them.
Source pages p. 648

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer sequence regarding the vision of Allah in the afterlife. The author presents a hypothetical dialogue: if the opponent admits that when the weakness (impairment of vision) is removed, one can see, then they affirm vision. If they deny, they are asked why since the obstacle is gone. The author then addresses the claim that removal of the pleasure of vision diminishes blessings. The response distinguishes between proving the Essence is visible (which is the real issue) versus the actual occurrence of vision in the afterlife. If the argument is about the latter, the objection is repelled. Further, even if someone is turned away from seeing Allah, Allah creates an opposite pleasure (like eating, drinking, marriage) so the person gains additional delight, not loss. An analogy is given: a gift of a thousand dinars plus a dirham is better than just a thousand. Finally, the author turns the argument against the opponent: if the pleasure of seeing the Prophet is among the best, then turning away from it would be a decrease; whatever they answer to that applies to the question about Allah.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The vision of Allah is the only source of pleasure in Paradise, so its removal would result in a net loss.
Correction: The author shows that if the vision is removed, Allah substitutes other pleasures (eating, drinking, marriage) so the person experiences an increase, not a decrease.

Checkpoint

A) He admits it is a decrease but necessary.
B) He argues that the pleasure is transferred to other delights, resulting in increase.
C) He denies that vision can be removed.
D) He says the question is invalid because vision is not a pleasure.

Key Takeaway
The author defends the vision of Allah by arguing that any loss of pleasure from vision is compensated by other delights, and by turning the argument back on the objectors using the Prophet's vision.

?
The author used the Prophet's vision as a mirror argument. If you were given the chance to see the Prophet in Paradise but then turned away to something else, would you feel it is a loss? Why does your feeling matter for how you understand Allah's generosity?

Refuting al-Qalanisi on Pleasure from Vision
Author refutes al-Qalanisi's claim that pleasure is generated from vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi rejection of generated pleasure avoids a logical problem that al-Qalanisi's view faces regarding the permanence of pleasure in the afterlife.

Core Idea
Generated pleasure ceases with its cause; Maturidi view allows enduring pleasure.

This passage examines a specific debate about the pleasure of seeing Allah in the afterlife. Al-Qalanisi claimed that the pleasure is generated (mutawallida) from the vision itself, which would mean it cannot persist if vision ceases. The Maturidi position rejects this generation, thus sidestepping the problem. Let us see how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the structure: first the opponent's view, then its consequence, then the Maturidi escape.
The passage is concise; every phrase matters.
2
Understand al-Qalanisi's claim
Al-Qalanisi asserts that pleasure is generated from vision and settles in the soul due to a natural faculty. Ask: what does 'generated' imply about the relationship between pleasure and vision?
Generated (mutawallida) means the pleasure is a direct effect of the act of seeing.
3
Identify the logical problem
If pleasure is generated from vision, then when vision ceases, the pleasure must also cease because a generated effect cannot exist without its cause. This would be problematic for the afterlife if the vision of Allah is intermittent or ends.
The problem is that the bliss of seeing Allah would be temporary and dependent on continuous vision.
4
Contrast with the Maturidi position
The author says the Maturidis do not hold that pleasure is generated. Therefore, they can conceive of pleasure existing even after vision is removed. This could be through Allah creating pleasure independently or sustaining it.
The Maturidi view thus preserves the possibility of permanent enjoyment even after the act of seeing ends.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this debate matters: it affects how we understand the nature of divine reward and the relationship between sensory experience and happiness in the hereafter.
This is a fine point of kalam that illustrates the rigor of theological reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم هذا الكلام ربما يرد على أبي العباس القلانسي حيث زعم أن لذة الرؤية متولدة من الرؤية تحل في نفس الناظر لقوة طبع في الحي الناظر، إذا كان الأمر كذلك عنده فلا يتصور حصول اللذة بعد زوال الرؤية المولدة اللذة، ولا وجود للمتولد بدون السبب المولد فأما عندنا إذا لم نقل بتولدها لتصور وجودها بعد زوال الرؤية فلا يرد علينا هذا الإشكال.
Then this speech perhaps applies to Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi where he claimed that the pleasure of vision is generated from vision, settling in the soul of the beholder due to a natural faculty in the living beholder. If the matter is according to him, then it is not conceivable to obtain pleasure after the removal of the vision that generated the pleasure, and there is no existence for the generated without the generating cause. But according to us, since we do not say it is generated, we conceive its existence after the removal of vision, so this problem does not apply to us.
Source pages p. 648

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific theory of Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi regarding the nature of the pleasure of seeing Allah in the afterlife. Al-Qalanisi held that the pleasure (ladhdha) is generated (mutawallida) from the vision itself, and it resides in the soul of the beholder due to a natural faculty. On this view, if the vision ceases, the pleasure must also cease because a generated thing cannot exist without its cause. The author points out that this leads to a problem: if vision is removed (e.g., if someone is turned away from seeing Allah), the pleasure would be lost. However, according to the Maturidi position (which does not adopt the theory of generation), pleasure can continue to exist even after the vision is removed, for example by Allah creating other pleasures. Therefore, the objection that the removal of vision entails loss of pleasure does not arise for the Maturidis.

Key Terms
متولدة
السبب المولد
رؤية
لذة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Maturidi view on vision implies pleasure is generated from vision.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the Maturidis do not say the pleasure is generated; they conceive its existence after the removal of vision. Therefore, the Maturidi position is that pleasure can persist even when the vision ends.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the problem of pleasure ceasing after vision does not apply to the Maturidi position?
A) Because the Maturidis deny that pleasure exists from vision.
B) Because the Maturidis do not hold that pleasure is generated from vision.
C) Because the Maturidis believe vision never ceases.
D) Because the Maturidis say pleasure is from a different source.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi rejection of generated pleasure avoids the logical problem that pleasure would disappear when vision ends, thereby preserving the possibility of enduring bliss in the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the pleasure of seeing Allah does not depend on the act of seeing itself but on His direct creation, does your hope in the afterlife rest on your own ability to perceive or on His unconstrained generosity? How does that shift your reliance today?
?
Al-Qalanisi believed pleasure is generated by vision, making it fragile and temporary. Do you sometimes treat your spiritual experiences as generated by your own efforts, and what would it mean to trust that Allah can sustain joy even when the means are gone?
?
The Maturidi view allows pleasure to endure after vision ends. Are there joys in your life that you assume will fade because their causes will fade? Would you dare to ask Allah to make them permanent through His power, not through their causes?

Refuting Ash'ari's Interpretation of the Vision Verse
Author refutes Ash'ari's interpretation using the verse's praise context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi scholar rejects al-Ash'ari's interpretation of 'لا تدركه الأبصار'.

Core Idea
A verse of praise cannot apply to all things.

Al-Ash'ari offered a clever interpretation of the verse negating vision of Allah, arguing it only negates perception by the eyes, not by the seer. His followers praised this as ingenious. But the author shows that this interpretation would make the verse meaningless praise, as it would apply to every created thing. Let's examine this critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage contains two clear parts: Ash'ari's claim and the refutation.
2
Identify Ash'ari's argument
Ash'ari distinguishes between 'eyes' and 'seer'. Find that distinction and understand why he thinks the verse does not apply to the dispute.
3
Understand the Maturidi critique
The author argues that the verse is praise. Ask yourself: if the negation only pertains to eyes, does that make Allah unique? The commentary will help.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تعلقهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿ لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ ﴾ فقد أجاب عنه الأشعري فقال : نحن نقول بموجب الآية فإن الله تعالى نفى الإدراك عن الأبصار لا عن المبصرين نحن نقول : لا يدركه البصر إنما يدركه المبصر فلم تتناول الآية محل الخلاف. وزعم الأشعري أن هذا جواب يعتمد عليه وتبجح أصحابه بهذا الجواب ويعدون هذا من حذاقته إلا أنا نقول : لا اعتماد على هذا الجواب لأن الآية خرجت مخرج التمدح وشيء ما لا تدركه الأبصار إنما يدركه المبصر فلا امتداح لله تعالى فيما يساويه فيه كل ما دب ودرج وعظم وصغر من أي جنس كان من الجواهر أم من الأعراض ، فكان صور الآية مبطلا هذا الجواب.
As for their clinging to His statement, the Exalted: 'Vision does not perceive Him', al-Ash'ari answered it by saying: We speak according to the import of the verse, for Allah the Exalted negated perception from the eyes, not from the seers; we say: the eye does not perceive Him, rather the seer perceives Him. So the verse does not encompass the locus of dispute. And al-Ash'ari claimed that this is a reliable answer, and his followers boast about this answer and consider it among his ingeniousness. But we say: there is no reliance on this answer, because the verse came in the context of praise, and a thing that the eyes do not perceive but the seer perceives—there is no praise for Allah the Exalted in what is equaled in it by every crawling, walking, large, and small thing, of any kind, whether from substances or accidents. So the form of the verse nullifies this answer.
Source pages p. 649

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash'ari interpretation of the verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' (Vision does not perceive Him) and offers a Maturidi critique. Al-Ash'ari argued that the verse negates perception from the eyes (basar) but not from the seer (mubsir). Therefore, the verse does not address whether the seer can see Allah; it only negates that the eyes perceive Him directly. The author reports that Ash'ari considered this a reliable answer and that his followers boasted about it. However, the author refutes this: the verse is phrased as praise (tamadduh). If the negation only applied to the eyes but not the seer, then every entity (be it substances or accidents) is such that the eyes do not perceive it but the seer does. Thus, this interpretation would not be particular praise for Allah, as it would apply to all things. Therefore, the form of the verse (its being a praise) invalidates Ash'ari's interpretation.

Key Terms
الأبصار
الإدراك
المبصر
التمددح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ash'ari's interpretation that the verse only negates perception by the eyes is a valid and clever answer.
Correction: The Maturidi critique shows that this interpretation makes the verse apply to all things, negating its purpose as exclusive praise of Allah.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject al-Ash'ari's interpretation of 'لا تدركه الأبصار'?
A) Because the verse is about the afterlife, not this world.
B) Because the interpretation would make the verse apply to all created things, negating its praise of Allah.
C) Because al-Ash'ari denied the vision of Allah entirely.
D) Because the verse clearly says 'لا تدركه' meaning absolute negation.

Key Takeaway
The verse's praise structure means its negation must be unique to Allah, not shared by all things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever taken a verse or attribute of Allah and rationalized it in a way that made it less awe-inspiring, just as Ash'ari did with this verse? What does that reveal about your reverence for Allah?
?
When you read 'لا تدركه الأبصار', do you feel a sense of distance or intimacy? How does the fact that this is a praise—not a limitation—change how you should feel about seeing Allah in the afterlife?
?
The author argues that if Ash'ari's interpretation were true, then every crawling thing would be equal to Allah in that respect. Is there any area of your life where you have made Allah's attributes 'common' by lowering them to your level? Repent and reclaim His uniqueness.

Nasafi's Critique of Ash'ari's Vision Verse Interpretation
Nasafi presents an objection, Ash'ari's answer, and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's refutation of al-Ash'ari's interpretation that the verse 'Eyes comprehend Him not' only negates comprehension by the eyes, not by the seer.

Core Idea
Ash'ari's answer fails because it makes the verse's boast apply to all creatures equally.

This passage presents a heated debate in Islamic theology: does the Quranic verse 'Eyes comprehend Him not' rule out seeing Allah in the afterlife? Al-Ash'ari offered a clever linguistic distinction, but the Maturidi theologian Nasafi dismantles it by examining the verse's rhetorical context. Read on to see how a single point about divine praise can overturn a major argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The verse 'Eyes comprehend Him not' is used as evidence that Allah cannot be seen. Read the first line of the passage to see how the objection is framed.
2
Examine Ash'ari's answer
Ash'ari distinguishes between 'eyes' (absār) and 'seers' (mubṣirūn). He says the verse only negates comprehension by the eyes, not by the seer. Find this distinction in the passage.
His followers praise this answer as a sign of his acumen.
3
Grasp Nasafi's refutation
Nasafi argues that the verse is a form of self-praise (tamadduḥ). If the verse only means that eyes don't comprehend Allah, that would be true for every object, no matter how small or insignificant. Thus the verse's boast loses its uniqueness.
4
Draw the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that the very form of the verse invalidates Ash'ari's answer. Reflect on why this is a strong critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يرد(۱) علينا هذا الإشكال. وأما تعلقهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿ لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ﴾ فقد أجاب عنه الأشعري فقال : نحن نقول بموجب الآية فإن الله تعالى نفى الإدراك عن الأبصار (لا) عن المبصرين نحن نقول : لا يدركه البصر (إنما) يدركه المبصر فلم تتناول الآية محل الخلاف. وزعم الأشعري أن هذا جواب يعتمد عليه وتبجح أصحابه بهذا الجواب ويعدون هذا من حذاقته إلا أنا نقول : لا اعتماد على هذا الجواب لأن الآية خرجت مخرج التمدح وشيء ما لا تدركه الأبصار إنما يدركه المبصر فلا امتداح لله تعالى فيما يساويه فيه كل ما دب ودرج وعظم وصغر من أي جنس كان من الجواهر أم من الأعراض ، فكان صور الآية مبطلا هذا الجواب.
This objection is raised against us. As for their reliance on His saying, 'Eyes comprehend Him not,' al-Ash'ari answered it, saying: We speak in accordance with the verse, for Allah the Exalted negated comprehension from the eyes, not from the seers. We say: The eye does not comprehend Him; rather, the seer comprehends Him. So the verse did not address the point of disagreement. Al-Ash'ari claimed that this is a reliable answer, and his followers boasted of this answer and counted it among his acumen. However, we say: There is no reliance on this answer, because the verse came in the form of self-praise. Any object that eyes do not comprehend but the seer comprehends is no praise for Allah the Exalted, since it is equaled in that by every creeping thing, great and small, of any kind, whether substances or accidents. Thus the form of the verse invalidates this answer.
Source pages p. 649

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the Ash'ari interpretation of the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' (Eyes comprehend Him not) and critiques the Ash'ari response. The passage begins by stating that an objection is raised. Then it recounts al-Ash'ari's answer: the verse negates comprehension by the eyes (al-absār), not by the seers (al-mubṣirūn). So the verse does not dispute the possibility of seeing Allah in the afterlife, because that would be seeing by the seer, not by the eyes. Al-Ash'ari's followers praise this as a clever distinction. However, the author (Nasafi) refutes it by pointing out that the verse is a form of self-praise (tamadduḥ). Any object that cannot be seen by eyes but can be seen by a seer is not a unique attribute of Allah, because all beings—from the smallest crawling creature to the largest—share this characteristic: they are not seen by the eyes but can be seen by a seer. Therefore, the verse's boast would be meaningless if interpreted this way. Hence the form of the verse itself disproves al-Ash'ari's answer.

Key Terms

الأبصار
المبصر
التمدح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Ash'ari answer is a strong linguistic point that preserves the possibility of seeing Allah.
Correction: Nasafi shows it fails because it undermines the verse's boastful tone—if the interpretation were correct, the verse would not be unique praise for Allah.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi reject al-Ash'ari's interpretation that the verse negates comprehension by the eyes but not by the seer?
A) Because the verse is about the afterlife, not this world.
B) Because the verse is a boast, and the proposed interpretation makes the boast apply to all creatures equally.
C) Because al-Ash'ari contradicted himself.
D) Because the seer and the eyes are the same.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes Ash'ari's answer by showing that interpreting the verse to negate only eye-comprehension strips it of its unique praise, as all creatures share that attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you ever find yourself forcing an interpretation to fit your preconceived beliefs, rather than letting the verse's own self-praise and majesty guide you? How might you change that?
?

?
Nasafi points out that Ash'ari's interpretation makes the verse's praise applicable to all creatures. Have you ever been satisfied with an explanation of a divine attribute that actually lowers Allah's uniqueness? What would it mean for you to truly let the Quran define Allah's attributes without human qualifications?

Restriction of Vision Verse and the Boast Objection
Ash'ari restricts the verse to this world; an objection based on tamadduh is answered.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari response to the vision verse involves a distinction between types of divine boasts, and how this defends the possibility of seeing Allah in the afterlife.

Core Idea
Not all divine boasts are equal—some are permanent, others can be restricted.

The vision verse 'No vision can grasp Him' seems to deny seeing Allah entirely. The Ash'aris argue it only applies to this world, because other proofs show vision in the afterlife. But opponents object: this would remove Allah's boast. In response, Ash'aris explain that boasts about Allah's essence are permanent, while those about actions can be restricted. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Notice the three parts: Ash'ari position, objection, and answer.
2
Identify the objection
The objector says restriction would remove the boast, and gives examples of boasts that cannot be restricted. Find the examples: 'لا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم', 'وهو يطعم ولا يطعم', 'وهو يجير ولا يجار عليه'.
These are all permanent boasts according to the objector.
3
Understand the Ash'ari answer
The Ash'aris classify boasts into two types: those about the essence or attributes (permanent) and others (restrictable). They show that the objector's examples are of the first type, so they are permanent. The vision verse is of the second type, so it can be restricted.
Pay attention to why each example is considered essence-related.
4
Reflect on the argument
Consider why this distinction is important for the debate on vision. How does it allow the Ash'aris to maintain both the verse and the possibility of seeing Allah in the afterlife?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعتمد الأشعري وأصحابه على أن هذه الآية وردت مطلقة، والدلائل الشرعية المثبتة للرؤية تثبتها في دار الآخرة فتقيدت هذه الآية بالدنيا ويكون محمول على أن الأبصار لا تدركه في الدنيا لقيام الدليل أنها تدركه في الآخرة. فإذا قيل لهم هذا تمدح وزوال ما به يتمدح لا يجوز لا في الدنيا ولا في الآخرة. ألا ترى أنه تعالى لما تمدح بقوله: ﴿ لَا تَأْخُذُهُ سِنَةٌ وَلَا نَوْمٌ ﴾ لا يجوز تقيد هذا بحال. وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَهُوَ يُطْعِمُ وَلَا يُطْعَمُ ﴾ لا يجوز أن يقال: لا يطعم في الدنيا ويطعم في الآخرة. وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَهُوَ يُجِيرُ وَلَا يُجَارُ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ لا يجوز أن يقال : لا يجار عليه في الدنيا ويجار في الآخرة. أجابوا أن ما تمدح الله تعالی به على وجهين: - منه ما كان راجعا إلى الذات أو صفة الذات ولا زوال لهذا القبيل لاستحالة العدم على ذلك لقدم ذاته وصفاته فلا يزول التمدح بقوله تعالى: ﴿ الْمَلِكُ الْقُدُّوسُ ﴾ لأنه راجع إلى الذات. ولا إلى التمدح بقوله تعالى: ﴿ لَا تَأْخُذُهُ سِنَةٌ وَلَا نَوْمٌ ﴾ فإنه راجع إلى صفات الذات لأنه بوجود السنة والنوم زال العلم وهو من صفات الذات فيستحيل زواله. وقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا يُجَارُ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ تمدح بكمال القدرة ولا زوال لها. وقوله: ﴿ وَلَا يُطْعَمُ ﴾ تمدح بالاستغناء عن الخلق وانتفاء الحاجة وذلك راجع إلى الذات لما أن الحاجة نقص والاستغناء مدح بكمال الذات.
Al-Ash'ari and his followers relied on that this verse came in an absolute form, and the legal proofs that establish vision (al-ru'yā) establish it in the abode of the afterlife, so this verse is restricted to this world, and it is taken to mean that eyes do not comprehend Him in this world because the evidence exists that they will comprehend Him in the afterlife. If it is said to them: This is a boast, and removal of that by which one boasts is not permissible, neither in this world nor in the afterlife. Do you not see that when He the Exalted boasted with His saying, 'Slumber seizes Him not, nor sleep,' it is not permissible to restrict this in any circumstance. Similarly His saying, 'He feeds and is not fed,' it is not permissible to say: He does not feed in this world and feeds in the afterlife. Similarly His saying, 'He protects and none can protect against Him,' it is not permissible to say: None can protect against Him in this world and they can protect against Him in the afterlife. They answered that what Allah the Exalted boasts about is of two types: One is that which pertains to the essence or an attribute of the essence, and this type does not cease, due to the impossibility of non-existence for that, because of the pre-eternity of His essence and attributes. Thus the boast in His saying, 'The Sovereign, the Holy,' does not cease, because it pertains to the essence. And similarly the boast in His saying, 'Slumber seizes Him not, nor sleep,' for it pertains to the attributes of the essence, because with the existence of slumber and sleep, knowledge would cease, and it is an attribute of the essence, so its ceasing is impossible. And His saying, 'None can protect against Him,' is a boast of perfect power, and it does not cease. And His saying, 'He is not fed,' is a boast of independence from creatures and the negation of need, and that pertains to the essence, because need is deficiency and independence is a praise of the essence's perfection.
Source pages p. 649

Commentary
This passage presents a second Ash'ari response to the vision verse and an objection based on the concept of boast (tamadduh), followed by the Ash'ari rebuttal. The first part states that al-Ash'ari and his followers argue that the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' is absolute but is restricted by the proofs for vision (ru'yā) in the afterlife. So it means that eyes do not see Him in this world, but they will in the next. Then an objection is raised: this restriction would remove the boast (tamadduh) of the verse, but a boast cannot be removed, neither in this world nor the next. The objector gives examples: 'لا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم' (He is not affected by slumber or sleep) cannot be restricted to this world; similarly 'وهو يطعم ولا يطعم' (He feeds and is not fed) and 'وهو يجير ولا يجار عليه' (He protects and none can protect against Him) cannot be restricted. The Ash'ari response is that the boasts of Allah are of two types: (1) Those that pertain to the essence (dhāt) or an attribute of the essence (ṣifat al-dhāt). These cannot cease because the essence and attributes are eternal. Examples given: 'الملك القدوس' (the King, the Holy) pertains to the essence; 'لا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم' pertains to attributes of essence (knowledge would cease if sleep occurred); 'ولا يجار عليه' is a boast of perfect power; 'ولا يطعم' is a boast of independence (istighnā') from creation, which pertains to essence because need is a deficiency. These boasts are permanent and cannot be restricted. (2) The other type is not explicitly stated here but implied; the verse about vision is presumably of a different type that can be restricted. The passage ends, but the argument is that the vision verse is not of the essence-pertaining type, thus it can be restricted.

Key Terms
الرؤية
التمدح
الذات
صفة الذات
القيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All divine boasts are equally unrestricted and cannot be applied to different contexts.
Correction: The Ash'ari response shows that boasts about Allah's essence or attributes are permanent and cannot be restricted, but boasts about actions (like vision) can be restricted to specific contexts without undermining the boast.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari response, why can the boast in 'لا تدركه الأبصار' be restricted to this world, unlike 'لا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم'?
A) Because 'لا تدركه الأبصار' is not a boast at all.
B) Because 'لا تأخذه سنة ولا نوم' pertains to the essence or an attribute of the essence and cannot cease.
C) Because the vision verse is ambiguous.
D) Because the Ash'aris reject the idea of restriction.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari response to the vision verse relies on distinguishing boasts about Allah's essence from boasts about His actions, allowing the verse to be restricted to this world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that Allah boasts of never slumbering or sleeping, do you truly entrust your life to His constant awareness, or do you still act as if He might miss something?
?
The Ash'aris argue that some of Allah's boasts cannot be restricted because they pertain to His essence—does your heart find rest in that unchangeable perfection, or do theological nuances make you doubt His absolute power?
?
If the vision verse were forever absolute and you could never see Allah, would your longing for Him remain as intense? How does this lesson affect your hope of meeting Him in the afterlife?

Objection and Answer on the Verse Denying Vision
Ash'ari objection from tamadduh and answer dividing tamadduh into two types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'aris defend the possibility of seeing Allah in the hereafter despite the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار', particularly through the distinction between praise pertaining to the essence/attributes and praise pertaining to actions.

Core Idea
Not all divine praise is eternal; some is based on temporal actions and can be removed.

This passage presents a classic theological objection and answer. The objectors argue that the verse denying vision is absolute praise, which cannot be restricted. The Ash'ari response distinguishes between two types of praise: one related to God's eternal essence and attributes, and another related to His temporal actions. This distinction allows the verse to be understood as referring only to this world, while vision in the hereafter remains possible.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and examples
Start by reading the objection from the Ash'aris and their opponents, along with the examples given (sleep, feeding, protection). Notice how they argue that restricting absolute praise is impermissible.
The examples are key to understanding the objection.
2
Identify the problem
Understand why the objectors consider it problematic to restrict the verse to this world: it would imply a change in God's praise, which is eternal.
This is the core of the objection: tamadduh cannot be conditional.
3
Examine the answer and its two categories
Read the answer carefully, noting the division of praise into two types: (1) related to the Essence or attributes of the Essence (eternal and unchangeable), and (2) related to actions (temporal and subject to change).
The classification is crucial for the resolution.
4
Apply the categories to the examples
Go through each example from the objection (sleep, feeding, protection, negation of perception) and see how the answer classifies them. Notice that some fall into the first category, others into the second.
The negation of perception is explicitly placed in the second category.
5
Understand the conclusion
Realize that because the negation of perception is action-based praise, it can be removed in the hereafter, thus reconciling the verse with the proofs for vision.
The proof of its removal is established by other evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأشعري وأصحابه على أن هذه الآية وردت مطلقة، والدلائل الشرعية المثبتة للرؤية تثبتها في دار الآخرة فتقيدت هذه الآية بالدنيا ويكون محمول على أن الأبصار لا تدركه في الدنيا لقيام الدليل أنها تدركه في الآخرة. فإذا قيل لهم هذا تمدح وزوال ما به يتمدح لا يجوز لا في الدنيا ولا في الآخرة. ألا ترى أنه تعالى لما تمدح بقوله: ﴿ لَا تَأْخُذُهُ سِنَةٌ وَلَا نَوْمٌ ﴾ لا يجوز تقيد هذا بحال. وكذا قوله تعالى: وَهُوَ يُطْعِمُ وَلَا يُطْعَمُ لا يجوز أن يقال: لا يطعم في الدنيا ويطعم في الآخرة. وكذا قوله تعالى ( وَهُوَ يُجيرُ وَلَا يُجَارُ عَلَيْهِ لا يجوز أن يقال : لا يجاز عليه في الدنيا ويجار في الآخرة. أجابوا أن ما تمدح الله تعالی به على وجهين: - منه ما كان راجعا إلى الذات أو صفة الذات ولا زوال لهذا القبيل لاستحالة العدم على ذلك لقدم ذاته وصفاته فلا يزول التمدح بقوله تعالى: الْمَلِكُ الْقُدُّوسُ لأنه راجع إلى الذات. ولا إلى التمدح بقوله تعالى: ﴿لَا تَأْخُذُهُ سِنَةٌ وَلَا نَوْمٌ . فإنه راجع إلى صفات الذات لأنه بوجود السنة والنوم زال العلم وهو من صفات الذات فيستحيل زواله. وقوله تعالى: وَلَا يُجَارُ عليه تمدح بكمال القدرة ولا زوال لها. وقوله: وَلَا يُطْعَمُ تمدح بالاستغناء عن الخلق وانتفاء الحاجة وذلك راجع إلى الذات لما أن الحاجة نقص والاستغناء مدح بكمال الذات. ومنه ما كان راجعا إلى أفعاله كقوله تعالى: الْخَلِقُ الْبَارِئُ الْمُصَوِّرُ فَإِن التمدح بذلك ما كان ثابتا في الأزل لحدوث أفعاله وما كان حادثا يجوز زواله فلا يبقى خالقا ولا بارئا ولا مصورا . والتمدح بقوله : ( وَهُوَ يُطْعِمُ وقوله : وَهُوَ يُجيرُ * من هذا القبيل. ثم التمدح بنفي الإدراك من هذا القبيل فإنه هو الذي يخلق الرؤية في عين من يراه فيمدح بأنه يخلق في عيونهم ضد رؤيته ولا يخلق رؤيته، وهذا من باب الفعل فيجوز زواله وقد قام دليل زواله في الآخرة.
Al-Ash'ari and his companions hold that this verse was revealed absolutely, and the definitive proofs for vision establish it in the abode of the Hereafter, so this verse is restricted to this world and is taken to mean that sights do not perceive Him in this world because the proof exists that they perceive Him in the Hereafter. If it is said to them: This is praise, and removal of that by which praise occurs is not permissible, neither in this world nor in the Hereafter. Do you not see that He, exalted, when He praised Himself by His saying: 'Slumber does not overtake Him nor sleep,' it is not permissible to restrict this in any way. Likewise His saying: 'And He feeds and is not fed,' it is not permissible to say: He does not feed in this world and feeds in the Hereafter. Likewise His saying: 'And He grants protection and none can grant protection against Him,' it is not permissible to say: None can grant protection against Him in this world and He is granted protection against in the Hereafter. They answered: That by which Allah exalted praised Himself is of two types: One type is that which pertains to the Essence or an attribute of the Essence, and there is no removal for this class because of the impossibility of non-existence for that due to the pre-eternity of His Essence and His attributes; thus the praise does not vanish by His saying: 'The King, the Holy,' because it pertains to the Essence. And the praise by His saying: 'Slumber does not overtake Him nor sleep' pertains to the attributes of the Essence, because with the existence of slumber and sleep, knowledge would vanish, and knowledge is among the attributes of the Essence, so its removal is impossible. And His saying: 'None can grant protection against Him' is praise by the perfection of power, and there is no removal for it. And His saying: 'He is not fed' is praise by independence from creation and negation of need, and that pertains to the Essence because need is deficiency and independence is praise by the perfection of the Essence. And another type is that which pertains to His actions, like His saying: 'The Creator, the Maker, the Fashioner'; indeed the praise by that was not established in pre-eternity because of the temporality of His actions, and what is temporal may be removed; thus He does not remain a Creator nor a Maker nor a Fashioner. And the praise by His saying: 'And He feeds' and His saying: 'And He grants protection' are of this type. Then the praise by the negation of perception is of this type, because it is He who creates vision in the eye of the one who sees Him, so He is praised that He creates in their eyes the opposite of seeing Him and does not create His vision, and this is of the category of action, so its removal is permissible, and the proof of its removal in the Hereafter has been established.
Source pages p. 650

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer regarding the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' (Sight cannot reach Him). The objectors (apparently Ash'aris or a group) argue that this verse is absolute praise (tamadduh) by God, and if it were restricted to this world, the praise would be removed in the Hereafter, which is impermissible. They support this with examples of God's eternal praise: not being overtaken by sleep, not being fed, and not being overpowered—all of which cannot be restricted to this world. The answer (أجابوا) divides the cases of divine praise into two categories: (1) Praise related to the Essence (dhāt) or attributes of the Essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt), which are eternal and cannot be removed, such as 'The King, the Holy' (al-Malik al-Quddūs), the negation of sleep (because it would imply removal of knowledge, an attribute of essence), the perfection of power in 'none can grant protection against Him', and independence from need in 'He is not fed'. (2) Praise related to His actions (af‘āl), which are temporal and can be removed, such as 'The Creator, the Maker, the Fashioner'—since actions are temporal, the praise can cease. The praise for feeding and granting protection is also of this type. The passage then specifies that the praise by the negation of perception (nafy al-idrāk) falls into this second category, because it is God who creates vision or its opposite in the eyes; thus the praise is based on an action (creating non-vision) and can be removed in the Hereafter. The proof of its removal has already been established.

Key Terms
تمددح
ذات
صفات الذات
أفعال
نفي الإدراك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All divine praise is equally eternal and cannot be restricted.
Correction: The Ash'ari answer distinguishes between praise related to eternal essence/attributes and praise related to temporal actions. Only the former is unchangeable; the latter can be removed.

Checkpoint
According to the answer in this passage, the praise of negating perception (nafy al-idrak) is categorized under which type?
A) It pertains to the Essence or attributes of Essence and cannot be removed.
B) It pertains to actions and can be removed.
C) It pertains to both depending on interpretation.
D) It is not considered praise at all.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari response to the objection uses a crucial distinction: praise related to God's essence or essential attributes is eternal, while praise related to His actions can be temporal and thus subject to change.

Maturidi Proof of Eternal Takwin from Tamadduh
Critique of the answer and Maturidi proof that takwin is eternal based on tamadduh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi school argues that God's attribute of making (takwin) is eternal, based on the impossibility of temporal praise implying benefit or deficiency.

Core Idea
Eternal praise demands eternal action; temporal praise would imply benefit and deficiency.

This passage presents a Maturidi critique of a response that only works under a different theological framework. The Maturidis use God's eternal self-praise as 'Creator, Maker, Fashioner' to prove that the attribute of making is eternal. If praise were acquired only when creation occurs, God would benefit from His own act—an impossible implication of deficiency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for the previous answer
The previous answer dividing praise into two types only works if one holds that attributes of action are temporal and that temporal causes of praise for Allah are permissible. Recognize this as a conditional statement.
2
Understand the Maturidi alternative
The Maturidis (our companions) affirm that takwin is distinct from the thing made, that action is eternal, the object of action is temporal, and praise is established in pre-eternity. They rely on this as evidence.
3
Follow the argument from tamadduh
If God's praise as 'al-Khaliq al-Bari’ al-Musawwir' were temporal, He would derive benefit from creating, implying that His action was done for His own benefit and that prior deficiency was removed. This is impossible for God.
The argument shows that temporal praise leads to an implication of need, which is incompatible with divine perfection.
4
Recognize the proof from the verse
The Maturidis use the same verse that others might use to argue for temporal praise, but they show that the verse's self-praise in pre-eternity actually supports the eternity of takwin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا أن هذا الجواب إنما يستقيم على أصل من يقول بحدوث صفات الفعل ويجوز حدوث أسباب التمدح الله تعالى. فأما على أصل أصحابنا القائلين بأن التكوين غير المكون ويقولون بقدم الفعل وحدوث المفعول وثبوت المدح له في الأزل ويجعلون هذا الحرف من الدلائل المعتمد عليها في تلك المسألة وهو أنه تعالى تمدح بقوله: ﴿ الْخَلِقُ الْبَارِئُ الْمُصَوِّرُ ولو حدث له التمدح بحدوث المحدثات لاستفاد بتخليقها مدحا واكتسب به نفعا فكان فعله حاصلا ليعود عليه به المنفعة، ولن يكون ذلك إلا بزوال النقص إذ لا شك أن كل ذات في حال لا يستحق مدحا إذ قوبلت به حالة استحقاقه المدح كان في تلك
Except that this answer is only correct on the principle of one who says that attributes of action are temporal and that the occurrence of causes of praise for Allah is permissible. As for on the principle of our companions who say that takwin (making) is other than the thing made and who say that the action is eternal and the object of action is temporal, and that praise is established for Him in pre-eternity, and they make this letter among the evidences relied upon in that issue—namely that He, exalted, praised Himself by His saying: 'The Creator, the Maker, the Fashioner.' And if praise occurred for Him by the occurrence of originated things, He would derive praise from their creation and acquire benefit thereby, so His action would be done for the purpose of returning benefit to Him, and that would only be by the removal of deficiency, since there is no doubt that every essence is in a state where it does not deserve praise; when it is compared to the state of deserving praise, it was in that state...
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This passage begins with a critical condition: the previous answer (dividing praise into two types) is only correct if one accepts the temporality of attributes of action (sifat al-fi‘l) and the possibility of temporal causes of praise. Then it contrasts the Maturidi position (here called 'our companions') who affirm that takwin (the attribute of making) is distinct from the thing made (al-mukawwan), that the action (al-fi‘l) is eternal while the object of action (al-maf‘ūl) is temporal, and that God's praise is established in pre-eternity. The Maturidis use the same verse 'al-Khāliq al-Bāri’ al-Musawwir' as a proof for the eternity of takwin. The argument goes: if God's praise by being 'Creator' etc. were due to the occurrence of created things, He would acquire benefit (manfa‘a) from creating them, which would mean His action was for the sake of returning benefit to Himself—implying a prior deficiency, which is impossible for God. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the point is that praise cannot be temporal without implying deficiency. This is a standard Maturidi argument for the eternity of the attribute of takwin.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The earlier answer about dividing praise into two types applies universally, regardless of one's view on divine attributes.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the answer is only valid for those who accept temporal attributes of action. For Maturidis, the eternity of praise is a proof for the eternity of takwin.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi position in this passage, why can God's praise as 'al-Khāliq al-Bāri’ al-Musawwir' not be temporal?
A) Because God's essence is eternal and any praise must be eternal.
B) Because if it were temporal, God would derive benefit from creation, implying deficiency.
C) Because the verse was revealed only in relation to the afterlife.
D) Because takwin is identical with the thing made.

Key Takeaway
God's self-praise as al-Khāliq, al-Bāri’, al-Musawwir in pre-eternity proves that His attribute of creating (takwin) is eternal, not acquired with time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you praise Allah as 'Creator', do you realize that this description was true for Him before any creation existed? Does this change how you understand His perfection and self-sufficiency – that His attributes are not dependent on His creation? Take a moment to repent of any thought that Allah became 'the Creator' only when He created.
?
If you were to catch yourself thinking that Allah does things to benefit Himself, how would this Maturidi argument confront that error? Will you now actively guard your heart against such subtle anthropomorphism, knowing that it implies deficiency in Allah?
?
This passage shows that God's self-praise is eternal, pre-dating all existence. Does your praise of Allah reflect this eternal reality, or is it only triggered by seeing His creation? Commit to praising Allah for His attributes even when you cannot see their effects – is your worship based on who He is, or only on what you experience?

The Maturidi Distinction Between Idrak and Ru'ya
Al-Nasafi presents the Maturidi distinction between comprehension and vision to resolve the apparent contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi school resolves the apparent contradiction between the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' and the scriptural proofs for the beatific vision by distinguishing between idrak (comprehension) and ru'ya (vision).

Core Idea
The verse negates comprehension, not vision; they are different.

Al-Nasafi presents a key Maturidi argument: the verse that seems to deny seeing God actually denies comprehensive perception, not vision itself. This distinction allows the Maturidis to affirm the beatific vision without contradicting the Quran. Let's examine the reasoning and its scholarly pedigree.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Al-Nasafi first reports the view of 'some of our companions' and then affirms it.
The passage ends with a list of scholars who adopted this answer.
2
Identify the key terms
Identify the two terms 'رؤية' and 'إدراك'. Notice how 'إدراك' is defined as 'إحاطة' (encompassment) and 'لحوق' (overtaking). These definitions are crucial.
Also note the terms 'تخصيص', 'تعميم', 'إطلاق', 'تقيد' which show the method of resolving apparent contradictions.
3
Understand the resolution
The verse negates idrak, which is defined as encompassment and overtaking—both impossible for God. The proofs for ru'ya affirm a different kind of perception. Thus no contradiction exists.
This resolution allows the Maturidis to accept both the verse and the scriptural proofs for vision.
4
Note the scholarly lineage
Al-Nasafi traces this answer to early Basran scholars and notes its adoption by al-Qalanisi and al-Maturidi. This shows the answer is not a novelty but part of a recognized tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعض أصحابنا قالوا إن مورد الآية في غير محل النزاع لأن النزاع وقع في الرؤية والآية وردت بنفي الإدراك ونحن كذا نقول: إن الإدراك منتف ولا كلام فيه فنحن قائلون بموجب الآية فقالوا بأن الإدراك هو الإحاطة واللحوق وهما منتفيان عن الله تعالى بالإجماع فأما الرؤية فثابتة لما ذكرنا من الدلائل السمعية، فإذاً لا تعارض بين هذه الآية وبين الدلائل المثبتة للرؤية لتوقف بينهما بالتخصيص والتعميم والإطلاق والتقيد بل هذه وردت بنفي غير ما وردت تلك بإثباته إذ الرؤية والإدراك غير - حكى الأشعري هذا الجواب في كتابه فرع نقض أوائل الأدلة على الكعبي عن جماعة من البصريين منهم عبد الرحمن بن أبي دؤيَّة وزهير الأثري وأبو معاذ التومني وأبو المغيرة البصري، وإلى هذا الجواب ذهب أبو العباس القلانسي حكي عنه ابن فورك وهو اختيار الشيخ أبي منصور الماتريدي- رحمه الله.
Some of our companions said that the context of the verse is not the point of dispute, because the dispute is about ru'ya (vision) while the verse came to negate idrak (comprehension), and we say the same: idrak is negated and there is no debate about it, so we are affirming the import of the verse. They said that idrak is encompassment (ihata) and overtaking (luhuq), both of which are negated of God by consensus. As for ru'ya, it is established by the scriptural proofs we mentioned. Thus there is no contradiction between this verse and the proofs that establish ru'ya, because there is room for specification and generalization, absolute and qualified. Rather, this verse negates something other than what those proofs affirm, since ru'ya and idrak are different. Al-Ash'ari narrated this answer in his book 'Far' Naqd Awa'il al-Adilla' against al-Ka'bi from a group of Basrans, including Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Du'ya, Zuhayr al-Athri, Abu Mu'adh al-Tummani, and Abu al-Mughira al-Basri. This answer was adopted by Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi, as narrated by Ibn Furak, and it is the choice of Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, may God have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi solution to the apparent conflict between the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' and the scriptural proofs for the vision of God in the Hereafter. The key is to distinguish between idrak (comprehension) and ru'ya (vision). The verse negates idrak, which is defined as encompassment (إحاطة) and overtaking (لحوق), both of which are impossible for God. However, ru'ya, which is a different kind of perception, is affirmed by other texts. Thus there is no contradiction; the two types of evidence address different things. Al-Nasafi notes that this answer has a pedigree: al-Ash'ari reported it from early Basran scholars, and it was adopted by notable figures such as al-Qalanisi and al-Maturidi himself. This establishes that the Maturidi school does not see a conflict.

Key Terms
رؤية
إدراك
إحاطة
لحوق
تخصيص
تعميم
إطلاق
تقيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' negates any possibility of seeing God, including the beatific vision in the afterlife.
Correction: The verse only negates comprehensive perception (idrak), not vision (ru'ya). The Maturidis affirm that believers will see God without encompassing Him.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi answer presented here, what does the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' actually negate?
A) Vision (ru'ya)
B) Comprehension (idrak)
C) Both vision and comprehension
D) Only the possibility of seeing God

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis resolve the apparent contradiction by distinguishing between idrak (comprehension) and ru'ya (vision), affirming that the verse negates only comprehending God, not seeing Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار', do you instinctively feel it limits God or protects your finite mind? Which assumption about God do you need to repent of—thinking you can fully comprehend Him, or doubting He can be seen at all?
?
The Maturidis held both that God cannot be encompassed and that He will be seen. What tension in your own life are you avoiding because you want a neat resolution? Will you trust the One who holds both truths even when you cannot reconcile them?
?
This lesson defines idrak as 'encompassment and overtaking'—trying to master or contain God. In what areas of your life are you subtly trying to control God, reducing Him to what you can handle? How will you surrender that today?

Al-Maturidi's Analogy: From Knowledge to Vision
Al-Maturidi argues by analogy that vision is possible despite negation of idrak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Maturidi's argument that negating idrak (encompassment) in the verse actually supports the possibility of seeing Allah, through an analogy with knowledge and encompassment.

Core Idea
Negating encompassment does not negate the act itself—a key insight from the analogy.

This passage presents al-Maturidi's incisive reinterpretation of a verse often cited against vision. He argues that idrak means full encompassment, and its negation leaves the possibility of vision intact, just as the negation of encompassment of God's knowledge does not negate knowledge itself.

Guided Path
1
Define idrak as encompassment
Read the beginning of the passage where al-Maturidi defines idrak as stopping at the extremities and boundaries, similar to encompassment (ihata).
Notice that this definition is crucial for the analogy.
2
Grasp the analogy with knowledge
Al-Maturidi draws an analogy: idrak is to ru'ya as ihata is to ilm. Negating ihata does not negate ilm; likewise, negating idrak does not negate ru'ya.
He supports this with Quranic verses affirming knowledge while denying encompassment.
3
Apply the analogy to ru'ya
Understand the conclusion: just as knowledge of Allah is established while encompassment is negated, vision of Allah can be established while idrak (encompassment) is negated.
This turns the verse from an objection into a proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنه رحمه الله حقق غاية التحقيق واستدل لصحة القول بالرؤية بهذه الآية لغاية حذاقته وتبحره في فنون المعارف فقال: إن الإدراك هو الوقوف على أطراف الشيء وحدوده ونهاياته كالإحاطة فكان الإدراك من الرؤية نازلا منزلة الإحاطة من العلم ثم بنفي الإحاطة لا ينتفي العلم. وقال الله تعالى يَعْلَمُ مَا بَيْنَ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَمَا خَلْفَهُمْ وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِشَيْءٍ مِّنْ عِلْمِهِ وقال وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِهِ عِلْمًا مع أنه تعالى قال فَأَعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا الله فكان العلم هو تبين المعلوم على ما هو به أو التجلي على ما مر في أول الكتاب. والإحاطة هي الوقف على حدود المعلوم ونهايته فكان العلم بالله ثابتا والإحاطة عنه منتفية، لاستحالة اتصافه بالحدود والأطراف والنهايات فكذا الرؤية به.
Then he (al-Maturidi), may God have mercy on him, achieved the utmost verification and used this verse to argue for the validity of the statement on vision, due to his great skill and depth in the branches of knowledge. He said: 'Indeed, idrak is the stopping at the extremities, boundaries, and ends of a thing, like encompassment (ihata). So idrak is to ru'ya as encompassment is to knowledge; by negating encompassment, knowledge is not negated.' And God said: 'He knows what is before them and what is behind them, and they do not encompass anything of His knowledge.' And He said: 'And they do not encompass Him in knowledge.' While He said: 'Know that there is no god but Allah.' So knowledge is the manifestation of the known as it is, or the disclosure as previously mentioned at the beginning of the book. Encompassment is the stopping at the boundaries and ends of the known. So knowledge of God is established, but encompassment of Him is negated, due to the impossibility of His being described with boundaries, sides, and ends. So likewise is vision of Him (ru'ya).
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage presents al-Maturidi's unique argument from the very verse that is often used to deny vision. He first defines idrak as the act of stopping at the extremities, boundaries, and ends of a thing—i.e., full encompassment (إحاطة). He then establishes an analogy: idrak is to ru'ya as encompassment (إحاطة) is to knowledge (علم). Just as the negation of encompassment of God's knowledge does not negate knowledge of God (as shown in Quranic verses that affirm knowledge while denying encompassment), so the negation of idrak (encompassment in vision) does not negate ru'ya (vision). Al-Maturidi supports this by citing verses: 'They do not encompass anything of His knowledge' (Q 2:255) and 'They do not encompass Him in knowledge' (Q 20:110), alongside 'Know that there is no god but Allah' (Q 47:19). Thus knowledge is affirmed while encompassment is negated. By analogy, ru'ya is affirmed while idrak is negated. This argument turns the objection into a proof: the very verse that denies idrak actually supports the possibility of vision.

Key Terms
إدراك
رؤية
إحاطة
علم
وقوف
حدود
أطراف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Negation of idrak in the verse means negation of ru'ya entirely.
Correction: Al-Maturidi shows that idrak means encompassment, and its negation leaves vision possible, just as negation of encompassment of knowledge does not negate knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is the basis of al-Maturidi's argument that the verse negating idrak actually supports vision?
A) He redefines ru'ya as encompassment
B) He draws an analogy between idrak/ru'ya and encompassment/knowledge
C) He argues that the verse is abrogated
D) He claims the verse is metaphorical

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi's argument turns the verse against idrak into a proof for the possibility of vision by distinguishing the act from its full encompassment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'No vision can encompass Him,' does your heart feel distant from Allah or does it yearn for a deeper encounter? How does al-Maturidi's distinction between idrak and ru'ya challenge your assumptions about what it means to see your Lord? What specific intention can you set today to cultivate the hope of that vision?
?
The passage shows that knowing Allah does not mean fully encompassing Him. How often do you fall into the comfortable illusion that your knowledge of Allah is complete? This lesson calls you to humility before the incomprehensibility of His being. What routine act of 'not knowing' can you adopt to acknowledge your limits daily?
?
Al-Maturidi's analogy relies on the Quran's affirmation of knowledge despite negating encompassment. Do you treat the attributes of Allah in your worship as a way to draw near without claiming to grasp? When you praise Allah for His attributes, do you feel the awe of encountering what you cannot fully grasp? What is one habitual prayer that you can deepen in light of this truth?

Ru'ya Established and the Verse Negates Idrak
Nasafi resolves verse contradiction by distinguishing ru'ya and idrak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Qur'anic verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' does not negate the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya), but rather negates comprehensive encompassment (idrak), and how this resolution is supported by early Sunni scholars.

Core Idea
The verse negates idrak, not ru'ya — vision and comprehension are distinct.

Imam Nasafi addresses an apparent contradiction: if Allah says 'No vision encompasses Him,' how can we affirm that believers will see Allah in the Hereafter? This lesson shows how the verse is reconciled with the scriptural proofs for ru'ya by distinguishing between vision (ru'ya) and comprehensive encompassment (idrak). The passage also traces this answer to major Sunni authorities including al-Ash'ari, al-Qalanisi, and al-Maturidi.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical structure: negations, then affirmation, then resolution.
2
Identify the two key terms
Find 'الرؤية' (vision) and 'الإدراك' (comprehensive encompassment) in the passage. Understand that the verse negates idrak, not ru'ya.
The author explicitly says 'الرؤية والإدراك غير'.
3
Understand the resolution method
The passage mentions 'التخصيص والتعميم والإطلاق والتقيد' (specification/generalization, absolute/restricted). This is how the contradiction is resolved.
This shows the verse is specific to idrak, while proofs for ru'ya are general.
4
Appreciate the historical consensus
Note the list of scholars who adopted this answer: al-Ash'ari, Basrian scholars, al-Qalanisi, and al-Maturidi.
This demonstrates the position is not isolated but widely accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهما منتفيان عن الله تعالى بالإجماع فأما الرؤية فثابتة لما ذكرنا من الدلائل السمعية، فإذاً لا تعارض بين هذه الآية وبين الدلائل المثبتة للرؤية لتوقف بينهما بالتخصيص والتعميم والإطلاق والتقيد بل هذه وردت بنفي غير ما وردت تلك بإثباته إذ الرؤية والإدراك غير أن - حكى الأشعري هذا الجواب في كتابه فرع نقض أوائل الأدلة على الكعبي عن جماعة من البصريين منهم عبد الرحمن بن أبي دؤيَّة وزهير الأثري وأبو معاذ التومني وأبو المغيرة البصري، وإلى هذا الجواب ذهب أبو العباس القلانسي حكي عنه ابن فورك وهو اختيار الشيخ أبي منصور الماتريدي- رحمه الله.
And they are both negated from Allah Almighty by consensus. As for vision (ru'ya), it is established due to the scriptural proofs we have mentioned. So there is no contradiction between this verse and the proofs establishing vision, because there is a specification and generalization, absolute and restricted between them. Rather this verse came negating what that verse did not establish, since vision and comprehension (idrak) are different. Al-Ash'ari narrated this answer in his book 'Far' Naqd Awa'il al-Adilla' against al-Ka'bi, from a group of Basrians, among them 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Du'ayya, Zuhayr al-Athari, Abu Mu'adh al-Tummani, and Abu al-Mughira al-Basri. Abu al-'Abbas al-Qalanisi adopted this answer, as narrated by Ibn Fawrak, and it is the choice of Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi – may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage begins by affirming that two things (likely direction and location, from previous context) are negated from Allah by consensus. It then asserts that ru'ya (seeing Allah in the hereafter) is established by scriptural proofs. The author addresses an apparent contradiction with the verse 'لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ' (No vision encompasses Him, 6:103). He explains that there is no real contradiction because the verse can be specified or generalized, or it is absolute while the proofs are restricted. The key point is that the verse negates idrak (comprehensive encompassment), not ru'ya (vision), since the two are distinct. The author then cites historical support: al-Ash'ari recorded this answer from a group of Basrian scholars, and it was also adopted by al-Qalanisi and al-Maturidi. Thus, the passage establishes the orthodox Ash'ari-Maturidi position that the verse does not negate the possibility of seeing Allah, only the possibility of fully comprehending Him.

Correction: The verse only negates comprehensive encompassment (idrak), not vision (ru'ya), as the passage explicitly states: 'الرؤية والإدراك غير'.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' negates comprehensive encompassment (idrak), not vision (ru'ya), and this resolution is supported by the majority of Sunni scholars.

Idrak Defined: Stopping at Limits
Definition of idrak and analogy with ihata and ilm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of idrak as stopping at limits, and the analogy between idrak:ru'ya and ihata:ilm, showing that negating idrak does not negate ru'ya.

Core Idea
Idrak is to vision as encompassing is to knowledge: negating one does not negate the other.

Imam Maturidi begins his proof for the possibility of seeing Allah by defining a key term: idrak (comprehension). He shows that idrak means stopping at the limits of a thing, similar to encompassing (ihata). This distinction is crucial because the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' only negates idrak, not ru'ya. In this lesson, we explore Maturidi's precise definition and his use of Quranic verses to establish that ru'ya remains possible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice the definition of idrak and the analogy.
2
Identify the definition of idrak
Find where Maturidi defines idrak. What does it mean to comprehend something?
Idrak is 'الوقوف على أطراف الشيء وحدوده ونهاياته' – stopping at sides, limits, ends.
3
Understand the analogy
Maturidi says idrak is to ru'ya as ihata is to ilm. Reflect on how this analogy works. If ihata is negated, is ilm negated?
Quranic verses show that Allah is known but not encompassed.
4
Apply the analogy
By analogy, negating idrak does not negate ru'ya. See how Maturidi concludes that ru'ya is possible while idrak is impossible.
5
Reflect on the consequence
Ask yourself: Why is it impossible to comprehend Allah? Because He has no limits. Yet vision does not require limits.
This sets the stage for the shadow analogy in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنه - رحمه الله - حقق غاية التحقيق واستدل لصحة القول بالرؤية بهذه الآية لغاية حذاقته وتبحره في فنون المعارف فقال: إن الإدراك هو الوقوف على أطراف الشيء وحدوده ونهاياته كالإحاطة فكان الإدراك من الرؤية نازلاً منزلة الإحاطة من العلم ثم بنفي الإحاطة لا ينتفي العلم. وقال الله تعالى: {يَعْلَمُ مَا بَيْنَ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَمَا خَلْفَهُمْ وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِشَيْءٍ مِّنْ عِلْمِهِ} وقال: {وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِهِ عِلْمًا} مع أنه تعالى قال: {فَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ} فكان العلم هو تبين المعلوم على ما هو به أو التجلي على ما مر في أول الكتاب. والإحاطة هي الوقف على حدود المعلوم ونهايته فكان العلم بالله ثابتا والإحاطة عنه منتفية، لاستحالة اتصافه بالحدود والأطراف والنهايات فكذا الرؤية به متعلقة لما قام من الدليل، والوقوف بالرؤية على حدوده وأطرافه ونهاياته مستحيل، لاستحالة الحدود والأطراف والنهايات عليه فتحصل رؤيته تعالى ويستحيل الإدراك كما أن الظل في يوم الغيم يرى ولا يكون مدركا لاستحالة الوقوف على أطرافه ونهاياته، وفي يوم الشمس يرى ويدرك لأنه ينتهي بالشمس فيوقف على [؟] ثم الآية خرجت مخرج امتداح ولا مدح في نفي الإدراك عنه مع كونه غير مرئي، لأن كل شيء لا يوقف على أطرافه ولا يدرك إلا بالرؤية، فإذا ما من شيء إلا وهو لا يدرك إذا لم ير فلم يكن الله تعالى به اختصاص فلم يحصل به تمدح، وإنما يحصل التمدح أن لو كان لا يدرك مع تحقق الرؤية فيه ولا يحاط مع تعلق العلم به فيكون ذلك إخبارا عن استحالة اتصافه بالحدود والنهايات التي هي من أمارات الحدوث وسمات النقص، فكان ذلك وصفا لذاته بالعظمة والكبرياء والتعالى عن سمات النقص وصفات الخلق، وإنما يكون هذا وصفا بما بينا أن لو كان الإدراك منتفيا مع تحقيق الرؤية فأما مع انعدامها فالإدراك منعدم لا لتبري الذات عن الحدود والنهايات والأطراف التي هي من أمارات الحدث بل لفقد سبب الوقوف عليها، فحينئذ لا يحصل به تمدح، والآية وردت مورد التمدح ولا تمدح ينفي الإدراك إلا وأن تكون الرؤية ثابتة، فدلت الآية من هذا الوجه على أنه تعالى مرئي. يحقق هذا أن لا تمدح بانتفاء الرؤية عن الذات لأن أكثر الأعراض عندهم لا ترى ولا تمدح لها بذلك، فدل أنه ما تمدح بانتفاء الرؤية، إذ لا تمدح بذلك وإنما تمدح بانتفاء الحدود والنهايات التي هي من أمارات الحدوث، وهذا لأن انتفاء أمارات الحدوث دليل على قدمه والقديم مستحق لصفات الكمال فصار في الحقيقة تمدحا بذلك.
Then he – may Allah have mercy on him – investigated to the utmost and used this verse to prove the correctness of the statement regarding vision, due to his great skill and deep knowledge in the sciences of knowledge. He said: Indeed, comprehension (idrak) is the stopping at the sides, limits, and ends of a thing, like encompassing (ihata). So comprehension is to vision as encompassing is to knowledge; then by negating encompassing, knowledge is not negated. And Allah Almighty said: 'He knows what is before them and what is behind them, and they do not encompass anything of His knowledge' (2:255) and said: 'And they do not encompass Him in knowledge' (20:110), while He Almighty said: 'So know that there is no deity except Allah' (47:19). So knowledge is the manifestation of the known as it is, or manifestation as mentioned at the beginning of the book. And encompassing is the stopping at the limits and ends of the known. So knowledge of Allah is established, while encompassing of Him is negated, because it is impossible for Him to be described with limits, sides, and ends. So likewise, vision (ru'ya) is related to Him due to the proof that has been established, but stopping by vision at His limits, sides, and ends is impossible, due to the impossibility of limits, sides, and ends for Him. Thus His vision is obtained, while comprehension is impossible, just as the shadow on a cloudy day is seen but is not comprehended due to the impossibility of stopping at its sides and ends, whereas on a sunny day it is seen and comprehended because it ends with the sun, so one stops at [؟]. Then the verse came in the mode of praise, and there is no praise in the negation of comprehension of Him while He is not visible, because every thing whose sides cannot be stopped at is not comprehended except by vision. Since there is no thing unless it is not comprehended when it is not seen, then Allah Almighty would have no distinction, and no praise would be obtained. Rather, praise would be obtained only if He were not comprehended while vision of Him is realized, and not encompassed while knowledge of Him is attached; then that would be an announcement of the impossibility of His being described with limits and ends, which are signs of temporality and marks of deficiency. So that would be a description of His essence with greatness, majesty, and transcendence above marks of deficiency and attributes of creatures. And this description only occurs as we have explained if comprehension is negated while vision is realized. As for when vision is absent, comprehension is absent not because the essence is free from limits, ends, and sides – which are signs of temporality – but due to the lack of the means of stopping upon them. Then no praise would be obtained. And the verse came in the context of praise, and there is no praise in negating comprehension unless vision is established. So the verse indicates from this aspect that He Almighty is visible. This is confirmed by the fact that there is no praise in negating vision of the essence, because most accidents, according to them, are not seen and have no praise for that. So it shows that there is no praise in negating vision; indeed there is no praise for that, but rather praise is for the negation of limits and ends which are signs of temporality. This is because the negation of signs of temporality is evidence of His preeternity, and the Preeternal is worthy of attributes of perfection. So in reality, it becomes praise for that.
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Maturidi's detailed investigation and proof for the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya) based on the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار'. He begins by defining idrak (comprehension) as 'الوقوف على أطراف الشيء وحدوده ونهاياته' (stopping at the sides, limits, and ends of a thing), which is like ihata (encompassing). He then draws an analogy: idrak is to ru'ya as ihata is to ilm (knowledge). Just as negating ihata does not negate ilm, so negating idrak does not negate ru'ya. He supports this with Quranic verses: Allah knows everything but nothing encompasses Him, yet knowledge of Allah is affirmed. Similarly, ru'ya can be affirmed without idrak. Next, he uses the analogy of a shadow: on a cloudy day, a shadow is seen but not 'comprehended' because it has no clear end to stop at; on a sunny day, it is seen and comprehended because it ends at the sun. Thus, ru'ya is possible without idrak. The main argument then shifts to the nature of praise in the verse. The verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' is praise (tamadduh). If Allah were invisible, negating comprehension would not be praiseworthy, since many invisible things are not comprehended. Rather, praise lies in negating comprehension despite the possibility of vision, indicating that Allah is seen but not encompassed. Negating comprehension while vision is absent would not be distinctive praise. Therefore, the verse indirectly affirms ru'ya. Finally, he reiterates that the negation of limits and ends is praise because it shows Allah's transcendence over created attributes, which are signs of temporality (huduth). Thus, the verse actually proves ru'ya by affirming that Allah is free from limits, which is possible only if vision is possible but encompassment is not.

Key Terms
الإدراك
الإحاطة
الرؤية
العلم
الحدود
النهايات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that idrak (comprehension) is synonymous with ru'ya (vision), so if Allah cannot be comprehended, He cannot be seen.
Correction: Maturidi shows that idrak is a specific type of comprehensive vision involving limits, which is impossible for Allah, but simple vision (ru'ya) remains possible.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is idrak (comprehension)?
A) Seeing something with the eyes
B) Stopping at the sides, limits, and ends of a thing
C) Knowing something completely
D) Having faith in the unseen

Key Takeaway
Idrak is stopping at limits; negating idrak does not negate ru'ya, just as negating ihata does not negate ilm.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about seeing Allah in the Hereafter, do you secretly feel it is impossible because your mind cannot grasp Him? How does distinguishing between seeing and comprehending (idrak) change the way you anticipate that meeting, and what will you do to cultivate that hope today?
?
This lesson teaches that negating idrak does not negate ru'ya. In your own life, do you limit your relationship with Allah because you feel you cannot fully understand His decrees or wisdom? What step can you take this week to trust Him more despite not 'encompassing' His plan?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's essence is beyond all limits and boundaries, how would that affect the way you speak about Him, worship Him, and rely on Him? What specific habit or assumption about Allah's 'closeness' might you need to reconsider in light of this truth?

Seeing Without Comprehending: The Shadow Analogy
Shadow analogy and initial praise argument that ru'ya must be possible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the shadow analogy that illustrates how something can be seen without being comprehended, and how this supports the possibility of seeing Allah.

Core Idea
A shadow on a cloudy day is seen but not comprehended – similarly, Allah is seen but not encompassed.

Imam Maturidi uses a vivid everyday example to clarify the distinction between vision and comprehension. Just as a shadow on a cloudy day can be seen but not fully grasped because it lacks a clear endpoint, so too can Allah be seen without being comprehended. This analogy makes the abstract argument concrete. Then Maturidi introduces a key argument from the nature of praise in the verse, showing that the verse must be praising something distinctive.

Guided Path
1
Read the shadow analogy
Read the passage and picture the two scenarios: cloudy day and sunny day. Notice the difference.
2
Identify why the shadow on a cloudy day is not comprehended
According to Maturidi, it is because it has no fixed end to stop at. Vision occurs, but comprehension fails.
This mirrors Allah: He has no limits, so He can be seen but not comprehended.
3
Understand the praise argument
The verse is praise (tamadduh). If Allah were invisible, negating comprehension would not be praise. So the verse implies ru'ya is possible.
Praise requires that 'comprehension negated despite visibility' – that is unique.
4
Connect to the overall proof
See how the shadow analogy and the praise argument together prove that ru'ya is possible while idrak is not.
